<p>The <b>Houston Rockets</b> are an American professional basketball team based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston, Texas</a>. The Rockets compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA), as a member club of the league's <a href="/wiki/Western_Conference_(NBA)" title="Western Conference (NBA)">Western Conference</a> <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Division_(NBA)" title="Southwest Division (NBA)">Southwest Division</a>. The team plays its home games at the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Center" title="Toyota Center">Toyota Center</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">downtown Houston</a>. The Rockets have won two NBA championships and four Western Conference titles. The team was established as the <b>San Diego Rockets</b>, an <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> originally based in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, in 1967. In 1971, the Rockets <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">moved</a> to Houston.</p>
<p>The Rockets won only 15 games in their debut season as a franchise in 1967. In the <a href="/wiki/1968_NBA_draft" title="1968 NBA draft">1968 NBA draft</a>, the Rockets selected <a href="/wiki/Power_forward_(basketball)" title="Power forward (basketball)">power forward</a> <a href="/wiki/Elvin_Hayes" title="Elvin Hayes">Elvin Hayes</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_first_overall_NBA_draft_picks" title="List of first overall NBA draft picks">first overall</a>, who would lead the team to its first <a href="/wiki/1969_NBA_Playoffs" title="1969 NBA Playoffs">playoff</a> appearance in his rookie season. The Rockets did not finish a season with a winning record until the 1976–77 season, when they traded for <a href="/wiki/Center_(basketball)" title="Center (basketball)">center</a> <a href="/wiki/Moses_Malone" title="Moses Malone">Moses Malone</a>. Malone went on to win the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="NBA Most Valuable Player Award">NBA Most Valuable Player</a> (MVP) award twice and lead Houston to the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Conference_Finals" title="NBA Conference Finals">conference finals</a> in <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_NBA_season" title="1976–77 NBA season">his first year</a> with the team. He also led the Rockets to the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> in <a href="/wiki/1981_NBA_Finals" title="1981 NBA Finals">1981</a> where they were defeated in six games by the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Larry_Bird" title="Larry Bird">Larry Bird</a> and future Rockets coach <a href="/wiki/Kevin_McHale_(basketball)" title="Kevin McHale (basketball)">Kevin McHale</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1984_NBA_draft" title="1984 NBA draft">1984</a>, the Rockets drafted center <a href="/wiki/Hakeem_Olajuwon" title="Hakeem Olajuwon">Hakeem Olajuwon</a>, who would be paired with 7 feet 4 inches (2.24 m) <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Sampson" title="Ralph Sampson">Ralph Sampson</a>, forming one of the tallest front courts in the NBA. Nicknamed the "Twin Towers", they led the team to the <a href="/wiki/1986_NBA_Finals" title="1986 NBA Finals">1986 NBA Finals</a>—the second NBA Finals appearance in franchise history—where Houston was again defeated by the Boston Celtics. The Rockets continued to reach the playoffs throughout the 1980s, but failed to advance past the second round for the rest of the decade. <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Tomjanovich" title="Rudy Tomjanovich">Rudy Tomjanovich</a> took over as head coach midway through the 1991–92 season, ushering in the most successful period in franchise history. Olajuwon-led Rockets went to the <a href="/wiki/1994_NBA_Finals" title="1994 NBA Finals">1994 NBA Finals</a> and won franchise's first championship against <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a>. <a href="/wiki/1995_NBA_Finals" title="1995 NBA Finals">The following season</a>, the Rockets reinforced by another All-Star, <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Drexler" title="Clyde Drexler">Clyde Drexler</a>, repeated as champions as the sixth seed in the West and swept the <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Magic" title="Orlando Magic">Orlando Magic</a>, led by a young <a href="/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal" title="Shaquille O'Neal">Shaquille O'Neal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penny_Hardaway" title="Penny Hardaway">Penny Hardaway</a>, in four games. Houston became the lowest-seeded team in NBA history to win the title.</p>
<p>The Rockets acquired all-star <a href="/wiki/Power_forward_(basketball)" title="Power forward (basketball)">forward</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Barkley" title="Charles Barkley">Charles Barkley</a> in 1996, but the presence of three of the NBA's 50 greatest players of all-time (Olajuwon, Drexler, and Barkley) was not enough to propel Houston past the Western Conference Finals. Each one of the aging trio had left the team by 2001, and the Rockets of the early 21st century, led by superstars <a href="/wiki/Tracy_McGrady" title="Tracy McGrady">Tracy McGrady</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yao_Ming" title="Yao Ming">Yao Ming</a>, followed the trend of consistent regular-season respectability followed by playoff underachievement as both players struggled with injuries. After Yao's early retirement in 2011, the Rockets entered a period of rebuilding, completely dismantling and retooling their roster. The acquisition of franchise player <a href="/wiki/James_Harden" title="James Harden">James Harden</a> in 2012 has launched the Rockets back into championship contention in the mid-2010s. The Rockets, under general manager <a href="/wiki/Daryl_Morey" title="Daryl Morey">Daryl Morey</a>, are notable for popularizing the use of advanced statistical analytics (similar to <a href="/wiki/Sabermetrics" title="Sabermetrics">sabermetrics</a> in baseball) in player acquisitions and style of play.</p>
<p></p>

<h2>Contents</h2>
</div>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_history">Franchise history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Franchise history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Houston_Rockets" title="History of the Houston Rockets">History of the Houston Rockets</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1967.E2.80.931971:_San_Diego_Rockets">1967–1971: San Diego Rockets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1967–1971: San Diego Rockets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elvin_Hayes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Elvin_Hayes.jpg/170px-Elvin_Hayes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Elvin_Hayes.jpg/255px-Elvin_Hayes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Elvin_Hayes.jpg/340px-Elvin_Hayes.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elvin_Hayes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hall of Famer Elvin Hayes was selected first overall by the San Diego Rockets in the 1968 NBA Draft.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Rockets were founded in 1967 in San Diego by Robert Breitbard, who paid an entry fee of US $1.75 million to join the NBA as an expansion team for the <a href="/wiki/1967%E2%80%9368_NBA_season" title="1967–68 NBA season">1967–68 NBA season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup> The NBA wanted to add more teams in the <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">Western United States</a>, and chose San Diego based on the city's strong economic and population growths, along with the local success of an <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team owned by Breitbard, the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Gulls_(1966%E2%80%9374)" title="San Diego Gulls (1966–74)">San Diego Gulls</a>. The resulting contest to name the franchise chose the name "Rockets", which paid homage to San Diego's theme of "a city in motion" and the local arm of <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics" title="General Dynamics">General Dynamics</a> developing the <a href="/wiki/SM-65_Atlas" title="SM-65 Atlas">Atlas missile and booster rocket program</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breitbard_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-breitbard-6">[6]</a></sup> Breitbard brought in <a href="/wiki/Jack_McMahon" title="Jack McMahon">Jack McMahon</a>, then coach of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Royals" title="Cincinnati Royals">Cincinnati Royals</a>, to serve as the Rockets' coach and general manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breitbard_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-breitbard-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The team, that would join the league along with the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_SuperSonics" title="Seattle SuperSonics">Seattle SuperSonics</a>, then built its roster with both veteran players at an <a href="/wiki/1967_NBA_Expansion_Draft" title="1967 NBA Expansion Draft">expansion draft</a>, and college players from the <a href="/wiki/1967_NBA_draft" title="1967 NBA draft">1967 NBA draft</a>, where San Diego's first ever draft pick was <a href="/wiki/Pat_Riley" title="Pat Riley">Pat Riley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breitbard_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-breitbard-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The Rockets lost 67 games in their inaugural season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> which was an NBA record for losses in a season at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1968, after the Rockets won a coin toss against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Bullets_(1963%E2%80%9373)" title="Baltimore Bullets (1963–73)">Baltimore Bullets</a> to determine who would have the first overall pick in the <a href="/wiki/1968_NBA_draft" title="1968 NBA draft">1968 NBA draft</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> they selected <a href="/wiki/Elvin_Hayes" title="Elvin Hayes">Elvin Hayes</a> from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston" title="University of Houston">University of Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Hayes improved the Rockets' record to 37 wins and 45 losses, enough for the franchise's first ever <a href="/wiki/1969_NBA_Playoffs" title="1969 NBA Playoffs">playoff</a> appearance in 1969,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69season_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-69season-13">[13]</a></sup> but the Rockets lost in the semi-finals of the Western Division to the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks" title="Atlanta Hawks">Atlanta Hawks</a>, four games to two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69season_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-69season-13">[13]</a></sup> Despite the additions of <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Murphy" title="Calvin Murphy">Calvin Murphy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Tomjanovich" title="Rudy Tomjanovich">Rudy Tomjanovich</a> and the management of Hall of Fame coach <a href="/wiki/Alex_Hannum" title="Alex Hannum">Alex Hannum</a>, the Rockets tallied a 57–97 record in the following two seasons and did not make the playoffs in either season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Because of the low performance and attendance, Breitbard looked to sell the team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup> and in 1971, Texas Sports Investments bought the franchise for $5.6 million, and moved the team to <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup> The franchise became the first NBA team in Texas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and the nickname "Rockets" took on even greater relevance after the move, given Houston's long connection to the space industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1971.E2.80.931976:_Improving_in_Houston_with_Murphy_and_Rudy-T">1971–1976: Improving in Houston with Murphy and Rudy-T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1971–1976: Improving in Houston with Murphy and Rudy-T">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before the start of the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_NBA_season" title="1971–72 NBA season">1971–72 NBA season</a>, Hannum left for the Denver Rockets of the <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association" title="American Basketball Association">American Basketball Association</a> – later renamed <a href="/wiki/Denver_Nuggets" title="Denver Nuggets">Denver Nuggets</a>, who <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABA%E2%80%93NBA_merger" title="ABA–NBA merger">joined the NBA</a> in 1976 – <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hannumrecord_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-hannumrecord-18">[18]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tex_Winter" title="Tex Winter">Tex Winter</a> was hired in his place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-winterrecord_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-winterrecord-19">[19]</a></sup> However, Winter's clashes with Hayes, due to a system that contrasted with the offensive style to which Hayes was accustomed, made Hayes ask for a trade, leaving for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Bullets_(1963%E2%80%9373)" title="Baltimore Bullets (1963–73)">Baltimore Bullets</a> at the end of the 1971–72 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was also around this time that the Rockets would unveil their classic yellow and red logo and accompanying uniforms used until the end of the 1994–95 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup> Winter left soon after, being fired in January 1973 following a ten-game losing streak, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Egan" title="Johnny Egan">Johnny Egan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Egan led the Rockets back to the playoffs in <a href="/wiki/1975_NBA_Playoffs" title="1975 NBA Playoffs">1975</a>, where the franchise also managed to win their first round against the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a>, subsequently losing to the veteran <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> in 5 games. At that time the Rockets gained popularity in Houston, selling out several home games during the regular season as the Rockets battled for a playoff spot and then selling out all of their home playoff games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1976.E2.80.931982:_The_Moses_Malone_era">1976–1982: The Moses Malone era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1976–1982: The Moses Malone era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_NBA_season" title="1975–76 NBA season">1975–76 NBA season</a> the Rockets finally had a permanent home in Houston as they moved into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Summit_(Houston)" title="The Summit (Houston)">The Summit</a>, which they would call home for the next 29 years. During the period, the franchise was owned by Kenneth Schnitzer, developer of the <a href="/wiki/Greenway_Plaza" title="Greenway Plaza">Greenway Plaza</a> which included The Summit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> After missing the 1976 playoffs, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Nissalke" title="Tom Nissalke">Tom Nissalke</a> was hired as a coach, and pressed the team to add a play-making guard in college standout <a href="/wiki/John_Lucas_II" title="John Lucas II">John Lucas</a> and a rebounding center through <a href="/wiki/Moses_Malone" title="Moses Malone">Moses Malone</a>, who he had coached in the ABA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-up_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-up-24">[24]</a></sup> The additions had an immediate impact, with the <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_NBA_season" title="1976–77 NBA season">1976–77</a> Rockets winning the Central Division and going all the way to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NBA)" title="Eastern Conference (NBA)">Eastern Conference</a> Finals, losing to the <a href="/wiki/Julius_Erving" title="Julius Erving">Julius Erving</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">Philadelphia 76ers</a> 4 games to 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1977%E2%80%9378_NBA_season" title="1977–78 NBA season">The following season</a> had the team regressing to just 28 wins due to an injury to captain Tomjanovich, who got numerous facial fractures after being punched by <a href="/wiki/Kermit_Washington" title="Kermit Washington">Kermit Washington</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers" title="Los Angeles Lakers">Los Angeles Lakers</a> and wound up spending five months in rehabilitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> After trading Lucas to the <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">Golden State Warriors</a> in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Rick_Barry" title="Rick Barry">Rick Barry</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> the Rockets returned to the playoffs in <a href="/wiki/1978%E2%80%9379_NBA_season" title="1978–79 NBA season">1978–79</a>, with "The Chairman Of The Boards" Moses Malone receiving the 1979 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_MVP" title="NBA MVP">MVP Award</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malonebio_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-malonebio-30">[30]</a></sup> but the team was swept 2–0 by Atlanta in the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Nissalke was let go, and assistant <a href="/wiki/Del_Harris" title="Del Harris">Del Harris</a> was promoted to head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1979 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_J._Maloof,_Sr." title="George J. Maloof, Sr.">George Maloof</a>, a businessperson from <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a>, bought the Rockets for $9 million. He died the following year, and while the <a href="/wiki/Maloof_family" title="Maloof family">Maloof family</a> expressed interest in selling the team, George's 24-year-old son Gavin took over the Rockets. A buyer was eventually found in 1982 as businessman Charlie Thomas and <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Shlenker" title="Sidney Shlenker">Sidney Shlenker</a> purchased the franchise for $11 million. The Maloof period of ownership marked the first dominant period of the Rockets,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thomas_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> highlighted by the team's first <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> appearance in 1981. Prior to the <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_NBA_season" title="1980–81 NBA season">1980–81 season</a>, the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">Dallas Mavericks</a> led to an NBA realignment that sent the Rockets back to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Conference_(NBA)" title="Western Conference (NBA)">Western Conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Houston qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1981_NBA_Playoffs" title="1981 NBA Playoffs">playoffs</a> only in the final game of the season with a 40–42 record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1981nbaseason_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-1981nbaseason-37">[37]</a></sup> The post-season had the Rockets beat the Lakers, in-state rivals <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_Spurs" title="San Antonio Spurs">San Antonio Spurs</a>, and the equally underdog <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Kings" title="Kansas City Kings">Kansas City Kings</a> to become only the second team in NBA history (after the <a href="/wiki/1959_NBA_Finals" title="1959 NBA Finals">1959</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minneapolis_Lakers" title="Minneapolis Lakers">Minneapolis Lakers</a>) to have advanced to the Finals after achieving a losing record in the regular season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1981_NBA_Finals" title="1981 NBA Finals">the final round</a> facing <a href="/wiki/Larry_Bird" title="Larry Bird">Larry Bird</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> in the finals round, the Rockets blew a late lead in Game 1 and won Game 2 at the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Garden" title="Boston Garden">Boston Garden</a>. However, afterwards the team failed to capitalize on the early success against the favored Celtics, and eventually lost in six games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>While new owner Charlie Thomas expressed interest in renewing with Moses Malone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thomas_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-34">[34]</a></sup> who had been again chosen as MVP in <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_NBA_season" title="1981–82 NBA season">1981–82</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malonebio_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-malonebio-30">[30]</a></sup> the Rockets traded him to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">Philadelphia 76ers</a> for <a href="/wiki/Caldwell_Jones" title="Caldwell Jones">Caldwell Jones</a>, as a declining regional economy made the Rockets unable to pay Malone's salary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matteroftime_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-matteroftime-40">[40]</a></sup> When the Rockets finished a league worst 14–68,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Celtics coach <a href="/wiki/Bill_Fitch" title="Bill Fitch">Bill Fitch</a> was hired to replace outgoing Del Harris,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matteroftime_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-matteroftime-40">[40]</a></sup> and the team won the first pick of the <a href="/wiki/1983_NBA_draft" title="1983 NBA draft">1983 NBA draft</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matteroftime_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-matteroftime-40">[40]</a></sup> used to select <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Sampson" title="Ralph Sampson">Ralph Sampson</a> from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Sampson had good numbers and was awarded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_Rookie_of_the_Year" title="NBA Rookie of the Year">NBA Rookie of the Year</a> award,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sampsonstats_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-sampsonstats-43">[43]</a></sup> but the Rockets still finished last overall, again getting the top pick at the upcoming <a href="/wiki/1984_NBA_draft" title="1984 NBA draft">1984 NBA draft</a>, used to select <a href="/wiki/Hakeem_Olajuwon" title="Hakeem Olajuwon">Hakeem Olajuwon</a> from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston" title="University of Houston">University of Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1984.E2.80.932001:_The_Hakeem_Olajuwon_era">1984–2001: The Hakeem Olajuwon era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1984–2001: The Hakeem Olajuwon era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1984.E2.80.931987:_The_Twin_Towers_era">1984–1987: The Twin Towers era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1984–1987: The Twin Towers era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_NBA_season" title="1984–85 NBA season">his first season</a>, Olajuwon finished second to <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a> in NBA Rookie of the Year balloting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and the Rockets record improved by 19 games, good enough for a return to the playoffs as the third best team in the West, where they were upset by the sixth-seeded <a href="/wiki/Utah_Jazz" title="Utah Jazz">Utah Jazz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The Olajuwon and Sampson duo earned much praise, and was nicknamed "Twin Towers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_NBA_season" title="1985–86 NBA season">following season</a>, Houston won the Midwest Division title with a 51–31 record. The subsequent playoffs had the Rockets sweeping the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Kings" title="Sacramento Kings">Sacramento Kings</a>, having a hard-fought six-game series with <a href="/wiki/Alex_English" title="Alex English">Alex English</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Denver_Nuggets" title="Denver Nuggets">Denver Nuggets</a>, and then facing defending champion Lakers, losing the first game but eventually managing to win the series – the only Western Playoffs defeat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Showtime_Lakers" title="Showtime Lakers">Showtime Lakers</a> – to get to the franchise's second Finals appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finals86_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-finals86-48">[48]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1986_NBA_Finals" title="1986 NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> once again matched the Rockets up against the Celtics, a contrast to Houston's young front challenging the playoff-hardened Celtics front court of Larry Bird, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_McHale_(basketball)" title="Kevin McHale (basketball)">Kevin McHale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Parish" title="Robert Parish">Robert Parish</a>. The Celtics won the first two games in Boston, gave the Rockets their only home playoff defeat that season in game 4, and clinched the title as Bird scored a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple-double" title="Triple-double">triple-double</a> on Game 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finals86_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-finals86-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_(ticket).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="652" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_%28ticket%29.jpg/125px-1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_%28ticket%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_%28ticket%29.jpg/188px-1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_%28ticket%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_%28ticket%29.jpg/250px-1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_%28ticket%29.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1987_NBA_Western_Conference_Semifinals_-_Game_2_-_Seattle_SuperSonics_at_Houston_Rockets_1987-05-05_(ticket).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A ticket for Game 2 of the 1987 Western Conference Semifinals between the Rockets and the Seattle SuperSonics.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Finals, Boston coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K.C._Jones" title="K.C. Jones">K.C. Jones</a> called the Rockets "the new monsters on the block" feeling they had a bright future. But the team had a poor start to the <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_NBA_season" title="1986–87 NBA season">following season</a> amidst players getting injured or suspended for cocaine usage, and during the playoffs were defeated in the second round by Seattle SuperSonics. Early in the 1987–88 season, Sampson, who had signed a new contract, was traded to the Golden State Warriors, bringing the Twin Towers era to an end just 18 months after their Finals appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Sampson's once-promising career was shortened due to chronic knee injuries, which forced his retirement in 1991. Jones' prophecy of a Rockets dynasty never materialized until the early 90's.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1987.E2.80.931992:_Lean_years">1987–1992: Lean years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1987–1992: Lean years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the next five seasons, the Rockets either failed to qualify for the playoffs or were eliminated in the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The first elimination in 1988 led to Fitch's dismissal, with <a href="/wiki/Don_Chaney" title="Don Chaney">Don Chaney</a> replacing him as head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chaneybio_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-chaneybio-55">[55]</a></sup> Chaney, also a former Celtic, had his best season during <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_NBA_season" title="1990–91 NBA season">1990–91</a>, where he was named the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Coach_of_the_Year_Award" title="NBA Coach of the Year Award">Coach of the Year</a> after leading the Rockets to a 52-30 record despite Olajuwon's absence due to injury for 25 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chaneybio_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-chaneybio-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Despite Olajuwon's usual strong numbers, the underwhelming roster could not be lifted out of mediocrity. However, the attempts to rebuild the team nucleus incorporated players that would later make an impact in the years to come, such as <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Smith" title="Kenny Smith">Kenny Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Maxwell" title="Vernon Maxwell">Vernon Maxwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Horry" title="Robert Horry">Robert Horry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Elie" title="Mario Elie">Mario Elie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Cassell" title="Sam Cassell">Sam Cassell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otis_Thorpe" title="Otis Thorpe">Otis Thorpe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Midway through the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_NBA_season" title="1991–92 NBA season">1991–92 season</a>, with the Rockets' record only 26–26, Chaney was fired and replaced by his assistant Rudy Tomjanovich, a former Houston player himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> While the Rockets did not make the playoffs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92year_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-92year-59">[59]</a></sup> Tomjanovich's arrival was considered a step forward. In the next year, the Rockets improved their record by 13 games, getting the Midwest Division title, and winning their first playoff series in 5 years by defeating the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers" title="Los Angeles Clippers">Los Angeles Clippers</a>, before an elimination by the SuperSonics during a game 7 overtime loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26,_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="494" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26%2C_2009.jpg/220px-Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26%2C_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26%2C_2009.jpg/330px-Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26%2C_2009.jpg/440px-Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26%2C_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rudy_T_Space_and_Missile_Center_Feb_26,_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rudy Tomjanovich spent all his playing career with the Rockets, and after becoming the team's head coach in 1992 led Houston to two straight championships.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1993.E2.80.931995:_Clutch_City_championships">1993–1995: Clutch City championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1993–1995: Clutch City championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On July 30, 1993, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Alexander_(businessman)" title="Leslie Alexander (businessman)">Leslie Alexander</a> purchased the Rockets for $85 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alexanderpurchase_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-alexanderpurchase-61">[61]</a></sup> In Tomjanovich's second full year as head coach, the Rockets began the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NBA_season" title="1993–94 NBA season">1993–94 season</a> by tying an NBA record with a start of 15–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Led by Olajuwon, who was named the MVP and <a href="/wiki/NBA_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award">Defensive Player of the Year</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hakeemaward_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-hakeemaward-63">[63]</a></sup> the Rockets won a franchise-record 58 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houstonindex_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-houstonindex-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94year_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-94year-65">[65]</a></sup> Aside from the second round which went through seven games against the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Suns" title="Phoenix Suns">Phoenix Suns</a>, the Rockets easily beat their Western Conference contestants during the <a href="/wiki/1994_NBA_Playoffs" title="1994 NBA Playoffs">playoffs</a> to advance to their third <a href="/wiki/1994_NBA_Finals" title="1994 NBA Finals">finals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a> opened a 3-2 advantage, but the Rockets managed to win the last two games on their home court and claimed their first championship in franchise history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houstonindex_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-houstonindex-64">[64]</a></sup> Olajuwon was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Bill_Russell_NBA_Finals_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Bill Russell NBA Finals Most Valuable Player Award">Finals MVP</a>, after averaging 27 points, nine rebounds and four blocked shots a game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hakeemaward_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-hakeemaward-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rockets initially struggled in the first half of the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_NBA_season" title="1994–95 NBA season">1994–95 season</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> which they fixed by sending Otis Thorpe to the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a> in exchange for Olajuwon's former college teammate <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Drexler" title="Clyde Drexler">Clyde Drexler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> With only 47 wins, the Rockets entered <a href="/wiki/1995_NBA_Playoffs" title="1995 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a> as the sixth seed in the Western Conference. Still, a strong playoff run that earned Houston the nickname "<a href="/wiki/Clutch_City" title="Clutch City">Clutch City</a>" had the Rockets defeating the West's top three seeds – the Jazz, Suns and Spurs – to reach back-to-back finals, this time against the <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Magic" title="Orlando Magic">Orlando Magic</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal" title="Shaquille O'Neal">Shaquille O'Neal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anfernee_%22Penny%22_Hardaway" title='Anfernee "Penny" Hardaway'>Anfernee "Penny" Hardaway</a>. When Houston swept <a href="/wiki/1995_NBA_Finals" title="1995 NBA Finals">the series</a> in four straight games,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> they became the first team in NBA history to win the championship as a sixth seed, and the first to beat four 50-win teams in a single postseason en route to the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-longroad_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-longroad-70">[70]</a></sup> Olajuwon was again the Finals MVP, only the second player after Michael Jordan to win the award two years in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1995.E2.80.932002:_Post-Championship_and_rebuilding">1995–2002: Post-Championship and rebuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1995–2002: Post-Championship and rebuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the offseason, the Rockets went for a change of visual identity, making navy blue and silver the new primary colors while adopting a new cartoon-inspired logo and pinstriped jerseys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barron.2C_David_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barron.2C_David-72">[72]</a></sup> The Rockets won 48 games in the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_NBA_season" title="1995–96 NBA season">1995–96 campaign</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96year_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-96year-73">[73]</a></sup> in which Olajuwon became the NBA's all-time leader in <a href="/wiki/Block_(basketball)" title="Block (basketball)">blocked shots</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1996_NBA_Playoffs" title="1996 NBA Playoffs">playoffs</a> had the Rockets beating the Lakers before a sweep by the SuperSonics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96year_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-96year-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the start of the succeeding season, the Rockets sent four players to Phoenix in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Charles_Barkley" title="Charles Barkley">Charles Barkley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The resulting "Big Three" of Olajuwon, Drexler, and Barkley had a strong debut season with a 57–25 record,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97year_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-97year-76">[76]</a></sup> going all the way to the Western Conference finals before losing to the Utah Jazz 4–2 on a dramatic last-second shot by <a href="/wiki/John_Stockton" title="John Stockton">John Stockton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_NBA_season" title="1997–98 NBA season">following season</a> was marked by injuries, and Houston finished 41–41 and the 8th seed, leading to another elimination by the top-seeded Jazz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Drexler retired after the season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and the Rockets traded to bring in <a href="/wiki/Scottie_Pippen" title="Scottie Pippen">Scottie Pippen</a> to take his place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In the strike-shortened <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_NBA_season" title="1998–99 NBA season">1998–99 season</a>, the Rockets lost to the Lakers in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/1999_NBA_Playoffs" title="1999 NBA Playoffs">playoffs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/1999_NBA_draft" title="1999 NBA draft">1999 draft</a>, the Rockets traded for the second overall pick <a href="/wiki/Steve_Francis" title="Steve Francis">Steve Francis</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Grizzlies" title="Vancouver Grizzlies">Vancouver Grizzlies</a>, in exchange for four players and a first-round draft pick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> However, after Houston traded a discontented Pippen to Portland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and Barkley suffered a career-ending injury,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> the rebuilt Rockets went 34–48 and missed the playoffs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> for only the second time in 15 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houstonindex_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-houstonindex-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_NBA_season" title="2000–01 NBA season">2000–01 season</a>, the Rockets worked their way to a 45–37 record. However, in a competitive Western Conference where seven teams won 50 games, this left the Rockets two games out of the playoffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In the following offseason, a 38-year-old Olajuwon requested a trade, and, despite stating their desire to keep him, the Rockets reached a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sign-and-trade" title="Sign-and-trade">sign-and-trade</a> agreement, sending him to the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Raptors" title="Toronto Raptors">Toronto Raptors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The ensuing <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_NBA_season" title="2001–02 NBA season">2001–02 season</a>—the first without Hakeem in two decades—was unremarkable, and the Rockets finished with only 28 wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.932009:_Return_to_Relevance">2002–2009: Return to Relevance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2002–2009: Return to Relevance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.932004:_Yao_Ming_arrives">2002–2004: Yao Ming arrives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2002–2004: Yao Ming arrives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg/250px-Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg/375px-Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg/500px-Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yao_Ming_free_throw.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Yao Ming during his rookie season with the Rockets.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Houston was awarded the first overall pick in the <a href="/wiki/2002_NBA_draft" title="2002 NBA draft">2002 NBA draft</a>, they selected <a href="/wiki/Yao_Ming" title="Yao Ming">Yao Ming</a>, a 7 feet 6 inches (2.29 m) Chinese center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Rockets missed the 2003 playoffs by one game, improving their record by 15 victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_NBA_season" title="2003–04 NBA season">2003–04 season</a> marked the Rockets' arrival to a new arena, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Center_(Houston)" title="Toyota Center (Houston)">Toyota Center</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newarena_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-newarena-92">[92]</a></sup> a redesign of their uniforms and logo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fashion_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-fashion-93">[93]</a></sup> and their first season without Rudy Tomjanovich, who resigned as head coach after being diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Bladder_cancer" title="Bladder cancer">bladder cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Led by former Knicks coach <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Van_Gundy" title="Jeff Van Gundy">Jeff Van Gundy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> the Rockets finished the regular season with a record of 45–37,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-04year_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-04year-96">[96]</a></sup> earning their <a href="/wiki/2004_NBA_Playoffs" title="2004 NBA Playoffs">first playoff berth</a> since 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houstonindex_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-houstonindex-64">[64]</a></sup> again losing to the Lakers in the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-04year_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-04year-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.932009:_Yao_.26_McGrady_duo">2004–2009: Yao &amp; McGrady duo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2004–2009: Yao &amp; McGrady duo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the offseason, Houston saw major changes in the roster as the Rockets acquired <a href="/wiki/Tracy_McGrady" title="Tracy McGrady">Tracy McGrady</a> in a seven-player deal with the Orlando Magic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The scoring champion McGrady and the strong rebounder Yao formed a well-regarded pair that helped the Rockets win 22 consecutive games in the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_NBA_season" title="2007–08 NBA season">2007–08 NBA season</a>, which was at the time the 3rd <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Basketball_Association_longest_winning_streaks" title="List of National Basketball Association longest winning streaks">longest winning streak in NBA history</a>. Still, the duo was plagued with injuries – of the 463 regular season games for which they were teammates, Yao missed 146 and McGrady 160 – and did not win any playoff series, despite gathering leads over the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">Dallas Mavericks</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_NBA_Playoffs" title="2005 NBA Playoffs">2005</a> and the Jazz in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_NBA_Playoffs" title="2007 NBA Playoffs">2007</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> After the 2007 elimination, Van Gundy was fired,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and the Rockets hired <a href="/wiki/Rick_Adelman" title="Rick Adelman">Rick Adelman</a> to replace him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TracyMcGrady.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="376" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TracyMcGrady.jpg/170px-TracyMcGrady.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TracyMcGrady.jpg/255px-TracyMcGrady.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TracyMcGrady.jpg/340px-TracyMcGrady.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TracyMcGrady.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Houston acquired Tracy McGrady in 2004.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the 2008–09 season, the Rockets signed forward <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ron_Artest" title="Ron Artest">Ron Artest</a>. While McGrady wound up playing only half the games before enduring a season-ending <a href="/wiki/Microfracture_surgery" title="Microfracture surgery">microfracture surgery</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> the Rockets ended the season 53–29, enough for the Western Conference's fifth seed. During the playoffs, the Rockets beat the Portland Trail Blazers four games to two, winning their first round since 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> During the series, <a href="/wiki/Dikembe_Mutombo" title="Dikembe Mutombo">Dikembe Mutombo</a> injured his knee, which forced him to retire after 18 seasons in the NBA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> However, the second round against the Lakers had the Rockets losing 4-3 and Yao Ming suffering yet another season-ending injury, this time a hairline fracture in his left foot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.932012:_.22Competitive_Rebuilding.22">2009–2012: "Competitive Rebuilding"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title='Edit section: 2009–2012: "Competitive Rebuilding"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NBA_season" title="2009–10 NBA season">2009–10 season</a>, the Rockets saw the departures of Artest in the offseason and McGrady, <a href="/wiki/Joey_Dorsey" title="Joey Dorsey">Joey Dorsey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Landry" title="Carl Landry">Carl Landry</a> during mid-season trades. Despite great play by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Martin_(basketball)" title="Kevin Martin (basketball)">Kevin Martin</a>, who arrived from the Kings, and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Brooks_(basketball)" title="Aaron Brooks (basketball)">Aaron Brooks</a>, who would eventually be chosen as the Most Improved Player of the season, the Rockets could not make it to the playoffs, finishing 42–40, 3rd in the Southwest Division. At that time, the Rockets set an NBA record for best record by a team with no All-Stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The Rockets would also finish ninth in the Western Conference for the following two seasons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> with Yao Ming getting a season-ending injury seven games into the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NBA_season" title="2010–11 NBA season">2010–11 season</a> and deciding to retire during the 2011 offseason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap_07202011_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap_07202011-109">[109]</a></sup> Said offseason, which saw the <a href="/wiki/2011_NBA_lockout" title="2011 NBA lockout">NBA going through a lockout</a>, had Adelman dismissed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and general manager <a href="/wiki/Daryl_Morey" title="Daryl Morey">Daryl Morey</a> deciding to start a revamp of the Rockets based on advanced statistical analytics (similar to <a href="/wiki/Sabermetrics" title="Sabermetrics">sabermetrics</a> in baseball) in player acquisitions and style of play. Kevin McHale was named head coach, and the roster saw significant changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreyball_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-moreyball-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="1175" height="351" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg/220px-James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg/330px-James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg/440px-James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:James_Harden_Rockets_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/James_Harden" title="James Harden">James Harden</a> arrived in Houston in 2012, and has since become a <a href="/wiki/Franchise_player" title="Franchise player">franchise player</a> for the Rockets.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.93present:_The_James_Harden_era.3B_Resurgence">2012–present: The James Harden era; Resurgence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2012–present: The James Harden era; Resurgence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the roster moves made by Morey during the 2012 NBA offseason,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreyball_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-moreyball-111">[111]</a></sup> only four players were left from the 2011–12 Rockets roster: <a href="/wiki/Chandler_Parsons" title="Chandler Parsons">Chandler Parsons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Smith_(basketball,_born_1991)" title="Greg Smith (basketball, born 1991)">Greg Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Morris_(basketball)" title="Marcus Morris (basketball)">Marcus Morris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Patterson_(basketball)" title="Patrick Patterson (basketball)">Patrick Patterson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> with the latter two leaving through trades during the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NBA_season" title="2012–13 NBA season">2012–13 NBA season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreyball_111-2"><a href="#cite_note-moreyball-111">[111]</a></sup> The most important acquisition was reigning <a href="/wiki/NBA_Sixth_Man_of_the_Year_Award" title="NBA Sixth Man of the Year Award">sixth man of the year</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Harden" title="James Harden">James Harden</a>, who Morey called a "foundational" player which he expected to be Houston's featured player after a supporting role in the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City_Thunder" title="Oklahoma City Thunder">Oklahoma City Thunder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Harden caused an immediate impact as part of the starting lineup for the Rockets, with 37 points, 12 assists, 6 rebounds, 4 steals, and a block in the season opener against the Detroit Pistons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> and an average of 25.9 points a game through the season. Combining Harden's performance and McHale's up-tempo offense, the Rockets became one of the highest scoring offenses in the NBA, leading the league in scoring for the majority of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreyball_111-3"><a href="#cite_note-moreyball-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2013_NBA_Playoffs" title="2013 NBA Playoffs">post-season</a>, the Rockets fell to the Oklahoma City Thunder in the first round, losing the series 4–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eager to add another franchise player to their team, the Rockets heavily pursued free agent <a href="/wiki/Center_(basketball)" title="Center (basketball)">center</a> <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Howard" title="Dwight Howard">Dwight Howard</a> in the 2013 offseason. He officially signed with the Rockets on July 13, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Led by the new inside-out combination of Howard and James Harden, and with a strong supporting cast including <a href="/wiki/Chandler_Parsons" title="Chandler Parsons">Chandler Parsons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Lin" title="Jeremy Lin">Jeremy Lin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%96mer_A%C5%9F%C4%B1k" title="Ömer Aşık">Ömer Aşık</a>, the Rockets were expected to jump into title contention in the upcoming season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> However, in the <a href="/wiki/2014_NBA_Playoffs" title="2014 NBA Playoffs">post-season</a>, the Rockets were defeated in the first round by the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a>, losing the series 4–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Still, in the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_NBA_season" title="2014–15 NBA season">2014–15 season</a>, without Lin and Parsons but reinforced by <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Ariza" title="Trevor Ariza">Trevor Ariza</a>, the Rockets started the season well, winning the first four games of the season for the first time since 1996–97,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> and winning each of their first six games by 10 points or more, the first team to accomplish this feat since the 1985–86 Denver Nuggets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> While the Rockets had many key players miss time throughout the entire season, James Harden took it upon himself to keep the Rockets near the top of the conference, turning him into an MVP front-runner. He became the first Rocket to score 50 points in a game since Hakeem Olajuwon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> as well as the only player in franchise history to record multiple 50 point games in a season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> On April 15, 2015, the Rockets beat the Jazz to claim their first ever Southwest Division title and first Division crown since <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Houston_Rockets_season" title="1993–94 Houston Rockets season">1994</a>, and by completing 56 wins finished with the third-best regular season record in franchise history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> During the playoffs, the Rockets beat the Mavericks 4–1 in the first round, and overcame a 3–1 deficit against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers" title="Los Angeles Clippers">Los Angeles Clippers</a> to win the Western Semifinals and return to the Conference Finals for the first time in 18 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In the Conference Finals, the Rockets were defeated by the Golden State Warriors 4–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_NBA_season" title="2015–16 NBA season">2015–16 season</a> saw <a href="/wiki/Kevin_McHale_(basketball)" title="Kevin McHale (basketball)">Kevin McHale</a> fired after a bad start where the team only won 4 of its first 11 games, and assistant <a href="/wiki/J._B._Bickerstaff" title="J. B. Bickerstaff">J. B. Bickerstaff</a> took over coaching duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Inconsistent play led to the Rockets struggling to remain in the playoff qualifying zone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> and surrounded by trade rumors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Houston only clinched its <a href="/wiki/2016_NBA_Playoffs" title="2016 NBA Playoffs">2016 playoffs</a> spot by winning its last game, finishing the season 41–41 to earn an eight seed and a match-up against the Warriors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Like in the previous year, the Rockets were once again defeated by Golden State in 5 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2016 offseason, <a href="/wiki/Mike_D%27Antoni" title="Mike D'Antoni">Mike D'Antoni</a> was named as the Rockets' new head coach,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> and Dwight Howard opted out of his contract's last year, becoming a free agent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In the following free-agency period the Rockets looked to embrace the play styles of both coach D'Antoni and Harden, through the signings of <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Anderson_(basketball,_born_1988)" title="Ryan Anderson (basketball, born 1988)">Ryan Anderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gordon" title="Eric Gordon">Eric Gordon</a>, two predominately perimeter players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season-by-season_record">Season-by-season record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Season-by-season record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_arenas">Home arenas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Home arenas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:453px;max-width:453px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:212px;max-width:212px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Summit,_exterior,_Houston.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="295" data-file-width="568" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/The_Summit%2C_exterior%2C_Houston.jpg/210px-The_Summit%2C_exterior%2C_Houston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/The_Summit%2C_exterior%2C_Houston.jpg/315px-The_Summit%2C_exterior%2C_Houston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/The_Summit%2C_exterior%2C_Houston.jpg/420px-The_Summit%2C_exterior%2C_Houston.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Summit (later Compaq Center) hosted the Rockets from 1975 to 2003, and was also the site where the Rockets won both of their NBA titles in 1994 and 1995. Today the site is the <a href="/wiki/Lakewood_Church" title="Lakewood Church">Lakewood Church</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:237px;max-width:237px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Center_entr.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3232" data-file-width="6048" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Toyota_Center_entr.jpg/235px-Toyota_Center_entr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Toyota_Center_entr.jpg/353px-Toyota_Center_entr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Toyota_Center_entr.jpg/470px-Toyota_Center_entr.jpg 2x" width="235"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Toyota_Center" title="Toyota Center">Toyota Center</a> is the current home of the Houston Rockets.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the four years the Rockets were in San Diego, they played their games in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Sports_Arena" title="San Diego Sports Arena">San Diego Sports Arena</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup> which had a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of 14,400.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> In their first season after moving to Houston, the Rockets did not have their own arena, and they played their first two years at various venues in the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Astrodome" title="Astrodome">Astrodome</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliant_Park#Reliant_Arena" title="Reliant Park">AstroHall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houston_Coliseum" title="Sam Houston Coliseum">Sam Houston Coliseum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hofheinz_Pavilion" title="Hofheinz Pavilion">Hofheinz Pavilion</a>, the latter eventually being adopted as their home arena until 1975. They also had to play "home" games in other cities such as <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waco,_Texas" title="Waco, Texas">Waco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque</a>, and even San Diego in efforts to extend the fan-base. During their first season, the Rockets averaged less than 5,000 fans per game (roughly half full), and in one game in Waco, there were only 759 fans in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their first permanent arena in Houston was the 10,000 seat Hofheinz Pavilion on the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston" title="University of Houston">University of Houston</a>, which they moved into starting in their second season. They played in the arena for four years, before occupying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Summit_(Houston)" title="The Summit (Houston)">The Summit</a> in 1975. The arena, which could hold 16,611 spectators,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> was their home for the next 28 years. It was renamed the Compaq Center from 1998 to 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronhistory_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-chronhistory-4">[4]</a></sup> Following the 1994 title, the Rockets had a sellout streak of 176 consecutive home games, including the playoffs, which lasted until 1999. However, the struggling 2000–01 and 2001–02 seasons saw Houston having the worst attendance average in the league, with less than 12,000 spectators each season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the 2003–04 season, the Rockets moved into their new arena, the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Center" title="Toyota Center">Toyota Center</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of 18,500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newarena_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-newarena-92">[92]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_NBA_season" title="2007–08 NBA season">2007–08 NBA season</a> where the team achieved a 22-game winning streak, the Rockets got their best numbers to date, averaging 17,379 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> These were exceeded once James Harden joined the team in 2013. The Rockets averaged 18,123 spectators during the 2013–14 season, selling out 39 out of the 41 home games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> 2014–15 had even better numbers, with 40 sellouts and an average of 18,230 tickets sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guideatt_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-guideatt-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_identity">Team identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Team identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms_and_logos">Uniforms and logos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Houston_Rockets&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Uniforms and logos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the Rockets debuted in San Diego, their colors were green and gold. Road uniforms featured the city name, while the home uniforms feature the team name, both in a serifed block lettering. This was the only uniform design the Rockets would use throughout their years in San Diego. The Rockets' first logo featured a rocket streaking with a basketball surrounded by the team name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breitbard_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-breitbard-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon moving to Houston in 1971, the Rockets replaced green with red.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup> They kept the same design from their San Diego days, save for the change of color and city name. The logo used is of a player with a spinning basketball launching upward, with boosters on his back, leaving a trail of red and gold flames and the words "Houston Rockets" below it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the 1972–73 season, the Rockets introduced the famous "mustard and ketchup" logo, so dubbed by fans, featuring a gold basketball surrounded by two red trails, with "Houston" atop the first red trail and "Rockets" (all <a href="/wiki/Capitalization" title="Capitalization">capitalized</a> save for the lowercase 'E' and 'T') in black surrounding the basketball. The initial home uniforms, used until the 1975–76 season, features the city name, numbers and serifed player name in red with gold trim, while the away uniforms feature the city name (all capitalized except for the lower case 'T' and 'N'), numbers and serifed player name in gold with white trim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1976–77 season, the Rockets modified their uniforms, featuring a monotone look on the <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Black" title="Cooper Black">Cooper Black</a> fonts and white lettering on the road uniforms. On the home shorts, the team logo is located on the right leg, while the away shorts feature the team name wordmark on the same location. With minor modifications in the number font, this version was used in all four of their NBA Finals appearances, including their <a href="/wiki/1994_NBA_Finals" title="1994 NBA Finals">1994</a> and <a href="/wiki/1995_NBA_Finals" title="1995 NBA Finals">1995</a> championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the 1995 title, the Rockets opted to modernize their look. After a fan contest with over 5,000 entries, the team went with the idea of <a href="/wiki/Missouri_City,_Texas" title="Missouri City, Texas">Missouri City</a> artist Thomas Nash of a rocket orbiting a basketball, which was then reworked by Houston designer Chris Hill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barron.2C_David_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barron.2C_David-72">[72]</a></sup> Nash would later sue the Rockets for <a href="/wiki/Breach_of_contract" title="Breach of contract">breach of contract</a>, given they were using his idea despite not having paid the contest prizes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The NBA suggested that the identity should follow the <a href="/wiki/Cartoon" title="Cartoon">cartoon</a>-inspired imagery that other teams adopted during the 1990s, leading to a rocket painted with <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">sharkmouth</a> <a href="/wiki/Nose_art" title="Nose art">nose art</a> orbiting a basketball. Red was retained, but navy blue and silver became the uniform's primary colors. Both the home white and away navy uniforms featured gradient-fading pinstripes and futuristic number fonts, with side stripes of navy fading to red. This was used until the 2002–03 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uniforms_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-uniforms-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intown_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-intown-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rockets' current logos and uniforms were introduced in the 2003–04 season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fashion_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-fashion-93">[93]</a></sup> created by New York-based agency Alfafa Studio in association with Japanese designer <a href="/wiki/Eiko_Ishioka" title="Eiko Ishioka">Eiko Ishioka</a>. The logo is a stylized 'R' in the shape of a rocket during <a href="/wiki/Takeoff" title="Takeoff">takeoff</a>, surrounded by a red orbit streak that can be interpreted as the central circle of a basketball court. Said "R" inspired the team's new custom typeface, designed so that every single digit could be read well from a distance, whether in the arena or on television. Red once again became the dominant color, with silver and black as secondary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> In 2009, the Rockets invoked the championship years with an alternate red uniform, featuring gold numbers and side stripes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ketchup_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-ketchup-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The Rockets had two sleeved alternate jerseys for the 2015–16 season, an alternate silver-colored uniform whose design referenced the design of NASA's <a href="/wiki/Titan_II_GLV" title="Titan II GLV">Gemini-Titan rocket</a>, and a red and gold jersey featuring the nickname "Clutch City".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1301" data-file-width="859" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG/220px-Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG/330px-Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG/440px-Houston_rockets_mascot.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

Clutch the Bear is the Rockets' mascot.</div>
